Vaidhy wrote:
> Isn't this discussion gone long enough?? Someone who wants an answer,
> asks a
> question.. If they do get the answer, they are happy.. if not, they ask the
> question again, rephrase it, translate it etc.. I am pretty sure all of us
> understand that if no answer is coming, it is because no one knows the
> answer or the question was not asked right. All these policy statements and
> nationalism is making me kinda scared....
> 

And tired ;-). It's a rather simple issue getting blown out of
proportion - just use what works. We all love our mother tongues, and we
use it where it's appropriate, and don't where it's not practical to do
so. I'm sure everyone of us wants to help the user at the end of the
day. Though I think typing a technical query in my mother tongue is more
trouble than it's worth, but if the user took the trouble to type it in
Tamil, perhaps he has his own reasons.

V.

On 01-Mar-07, at 1:56 AM, Manoj Srivastava wrote:

>> Though I think typing a technical query in my mother tongue is more
>> trouble than it's worth, but if the user took the trouble to type it
>> in Tamil, perhaps he has his own reasons.
>
>         This is a point. I don't think I can ask, or answer, a
>  question in my mother tongue. I mean, what is the hindi of file?
>  directory? configuration file? script? program? how do I say init
>  script in Hindi? or tamil?

language of a list/channel or the like is decided by the admins - or  
the people who created it. This is usualy mentioned in the list  
rules. If there is sufficient demand for a new language, a new list  
gets created. This also governs international lists - like postgresql  
or python, for all one knows, the non-english speakers may be the  
majority, but they have to take the trouble to learn english. I have  
been trying to put together a hacker dictionary in various Indian  
languages and my experience shows that our languages are never going  
to catch up with the new terminology. At the most what we do is  
combine english and the local language. And I have noticed this kind  
of combination is there in popular local language publications when  
dealing with computers/software. I have also seen this in local  
language versions of manuals - for example the manual that comes with  
the Tata Sky package. We may not like the idea, but it is impossible  
in todays world to write/learn to write good code without a good  
command of english.

-- 

regards
kg

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Mar  1 09:02:21 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Mar  1 09:03:15 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Monthly reminder: mailing list guidelines
Message-ID: <341165.7722.qm@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>

This is a monthly reminder on the mail posting
guidelines:

1. Use a proper subject line.

2. Do not troll in the mailing list

Link: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_troll

3. Use [OT] for off-topic, non-technical discussions.
But, don't misuse this to start flame wars or to troll
in the mailing list.

4. Do not top-post:

Link: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Top-posting

Example of a top-post:

   Because it messes up the order in which 
   people normally read text.
   > > Why is top-posting 
   > > such a bad thing?
   Top-posting.
   > > What is the most 
   > > annoying thing in e-mail?

Always use interleaved posting. Trim the post you are
replying to and interleave your replies so that each
part of the reply is under the quoted part that you
are replying to. Further please leave a gap of one
line between the matter you are quoting and your
reply.

   what is your name?
   regards
   xyz

trimmed and replied as:

    >what is your name?

    my name is ilugc

and not as:

   >what is your name?
   >regards
   >xyz
   my name is ilugc.

5. Do not over-quote:

Example of an over-quote:

>>> On Friday you said
>>>  blah blah blah
>> On Saturday you said
>>  foo foo foo
> On Sunday you said
>  foobar

6. Do not post HTML messages

7. Do not recycle messages

8. Do not send attachments

9. Do not attach obnoxious, nonsensical legal
disclaimers. If your company uses disclaimers, don't
use your company ID for the mailing list.

10. Do not reply to a digest. (If you are in digest
mode and want to reply to a post use ILUGC Gmane blog
interface.

Link:
http://blog.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc

11. Search for answers for your questions/problems in
google.com or any other search engine before posting
your query to the mailing list.

If any of the above are not clear to you, Please read
the detailed list guidelines:

Link:
http://www.catb.org/~esr/faqs/smart-questions.html

12. Do not post messages in all capital letters. Mails
in CAPS is considered rude and is similar to shouting
during a conversation.

13. If you or your company is into GNU/Linux
migration, or you want help into GNU/Linux migration,
check here:
http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/?title=GNU_Linux_migration

14. If you are looking for GNU/Linux distro CDs please
check here:
http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/?title=CDs_for_Grab

15. Following these guidelines could be helpful
http://people.debian.org/~enrico/dcg/

16. Don't send season's greetings or birthday invites
to the group. Its not mailing list etiquette.

We must use the above guidelines to maintain better
readability, proper archives, efficient bandwidth
usage, etc.


 
____________________________________________________________________________________
Need a quick answer? Get one in minutes from people who know.
Ask your question on www.Answers.yahoo.com

Sometime on Thursday 01 March 2007 16:00, vasudevan rk said:
> We are using LAMP technologies in our RHEL-4 & CentOS-4 Server, so that we
> need Anti-Virus to protect our files and databases too.

What you need to do is server hardening, limit access to the server, choosing 
right web applications, applying security updates in time, et. al. and not an 
antivirus.

Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
> if you are using dynamic IP keep rebooting the modem until you get a
> clean IP, and then dont switch off

Limited use strategy

BSNL has only a limited range of dynamic IPs - and blocks on dynamic IP
space is often by the /24 (255 IPs around your IP) and higher levels.

Easier to get off bsnl.

On Thu, 1 Mar 2007, Srinivasan R wrote:

I use Hathway @ Home. Try the following

1. Check the System/Gateway IP. (Check the Call Center)
2. Get the correct DNS IPs and set it in /etc/resolv.conf
3. Check the Rx count in ifconfig output.

Finally, check the earth connection of your PC, if it is not proper,
you will get this kind of misbehaviors.

Bye :)

Bharathi S

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Fri Mar  2 12:53:22 2007
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)
Date: Fri Mar  2 12:53:56 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] How to convert Photos to VCD in Linux?
In-Reply-To: <200703021126.37351.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070302072323.38057.qmail@web7901.mail.in.yahoo.com>


--- Shrinivasan T <tshrinivasan@gmail.com> wrote:

> Friends.
> 
> I have a digital camera.
> I took lot of Photos. Store and view in computers.
> 
> But, I want to show the photos to my friends who dont have
> computers?
> I burh the photos in normal data mode only.
> The Latest DVD players connected with TV, show the photos as
> slideshows.
> 
> But the old VCD players can not show them.
> So, I want to convert the photos into video format.
> The I can burn the video into CD and can plany in normal VCD
> players.
> 
> How to convert photos into video format?
> 
> I googled, but only windows software are resulting.
> 
> Please help me to do this.
> 
> Thanks.
> T.Shrinivasan.
> 
ImageMagick has good conversion tool.
e.g
convert -dealy 200 *.jpg video.mpg

will convert all pictures with jpg extension into mpg stream with 2
seconds delay [note: delay is in 1/100 of sec].
For more info look at man convert and man ImageMagick

Raman.P

From gsk_samy at yahoo.com  Fri Mar  2 15:10:26 2007

-> ImageMagick has good conversion tool.
> e.g > convert -dealy 200 *.jpg video.mpg
> 
> will convert all pictures with jpg extension into
> mpg stream with 2> seconds delay [note: delay is in

In ImageMagick-6.3.1-Q16 :

convert -adjoin -delay 200 file1.jpg file2.jpg
new.mpeg 

Refer:

http://www.imagemagick.org/pipermail/
magick-users/2002-February/000921.html

   Register Now for the Red Hat Challenge

   This is your special invitation to participate in the Red Hat
   Challenge. The Challenge provides a chance for technology-savvy
   business and design school students from top graduate schools
   in select countries to compete for a $20,000 grand prize and
   a trip to San Diego for the Red Hat Summit.

   In addition to the prizes, the Red Hat Challenge provides a
   unique way for you to demonstrate innovative thinking to the
   leader in open source software and be considered for intern
   and full-time positions.

   You'll be asked to submit a 3-5 page concept plan in response
   to Red Hat's challenge question. Judged by a panel of open source
   software industry experts, you'll have an opportunity to research
   and brainstorm innovative solutions to a real-world business challenge.

   The winning concept and university will be recognized on stage
   before the open source community at the Red Hat Summit in San Diego,
   California.

i get the same. What had happened was that the remote server did not  
have X11. As it shouldnt. So when the program asked for an X11  
library, I assumed that I would have to install X11 also in order to  
get the library wanted. And a search for x11 did not reveal any  
libxt6. Anyway, someone told me to just install that library, which I  
did. It then went on the demand a few more libraries and the,  
mercifully, stopped asking. Just shows that often an approach to a  
solution is coloured by the context in which the problem arises.  
Context here being appalled at the waste of effort installing X in a  
remote server.

** WARNING **: oss_open(): Failed to open audio device (/dev/dsp):

closing apps and on such conditions I can hear the associated sounds
from the speakers.

00:10.1 Audio device: nVidia Corporation MCP51 High Definition Audio (rev a2)
        Subsystem: Giga-byte Technology Unknown device a102
        Control: I/O- Mem+ BusMaster+ SpecCycle- MemWINV- VGASnoop-
ParErr- Stepping- SERR- FastB2B-

From sbharathi at MidasComm.com  Sun Mar  4 16:23:32 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Sun Mar  4 16:24:14 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] : Audio Problems with nViDia
Message-ID: <32820.203.212.230.148.1173005612.squirrel@203.212.230.148>

> Problem is : unable to play any kind of audio files (right plugins
for
> mp3 / ogg / vorbis are available too).

KDE will run 'artsd', which used to hold the /dev/dsp. So kill that
deamon and try to run music player OR give all access /dev/dsp to
everyone and try.

HTH :)

Bharathi S

>> mp3 / ogg / vorbis are available too).

> KDE will run 'artsd', which used to hold the /dev/dsp. So kill that
> deamon and try to run music player OR give all access /dev/dsp to
> everyone and try.

Dont change the permissions of /dev/dsp

Add whichever user you want to play music as to group "audio"

As simple as that.

hi suresh,

On 3/5/07, Suresh Kumar <suresh1876@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> yes tried that..
>
> mysql -u mysql -p podslam < feb_25_mysql.dump
>
> but i get error..
> saying " Access denied for user ''@'localhost' to database 'podslam'"
>
> and again when i tried using root user
>
> i got .
>
> " ERROR at line 1: Unknown command ''.               "


Edit the dump file. Delete all lines other  than DMLs and DDLs. Save it and
try as  you did a bove.


Another way to import dumps:
mysql -u root -p databasename
After fetching the password, You will be dropped into mysql console.

In the console type:
source filenamewithfullpath

eg.,
mysql > source /tmp/mysqldump.dump


regards,
Ignacius

>> Problem is : unable to play any kind of audio files (right plugins

>> mp3 / ogg / vorbis are available too).

> KDE will run 'artsd', which used to hold the /dev/dsp. So kill that

lsof /dev/snd* /dev/dsp

^ ^ the above command will show all processes holding control of the 
audio device.

From vijaysanand2002 at yahoo.com  Tue Mar  6 09:50:16 2007
From: vijaysanand2002 at yahoo.com (Vijay S Anand)
Date: Tue Mar  6 09:50:59 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux distribution Server
Message-ID: <382380.56840.qm@web36802.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

Hello Everyone,

My name is Vijay and I am involved with IIT in a number of their projects and working with the TeNeT group since I came back from Canada about a year or so ago. I used to be part of the organizers group running the linux/unix users group there, and was quite involved with the community.

In any case, I have been getting back to linux (as I am getting involved with some development work) and one of the things I notice when updating and downloading from distro mirrors is the lack of any Indian distribution server. When Indonesia has a few, its sad that there is not even one for India.

I have been talking to Atul Chitnis about it, and we are trying to do something on behalf of FOSS.in. A few days ago I came across an ftp running in IITM (ironically) which had some distros on them - though it didnt seem like it was synced regularly with the master servers. We are trying to see if there is something we can formalize with IITM, or maybe start fresh with servers and bandwidth.

I would like the support of the local LUG chapter in this regard, and anything we can all contribute towards this goal. Ofcourse, your suggestions would be quite welcome as well.

You can reach me at vijay@vijayanand.name for a speedier response.

I look forward to hearing from you, and hope to meet you guys in one of the meets these days.

Regards,
Vijay

Vijay S Anand wrote:

> In any case, I have been getting back to linux (as I am getting
> involved with some development work) and one of the things I notice
> when updating and downloading from distro mirrors is the lack of any
> Indian distribution server. When Indonesia has a few, its sad that
> there is not even one for India.

Oh - one more reality check about the lack of mirrors in India.

Given the way the Internet in India is built up [not very much peering
at all, despite having a "national internet exchange" up, running and
exchanging derisory amounts of traffic] - it is often far faster to sync
from a mirror in singapore or hong kong depending on where your ISP gets
upstream connectivity from.  Even for me - and I live in Adyar, less
than three or four miles from the IIT campus.

ps:

> Canada about a year or so ago. I used to be part of the organizers
> group running the linux/unix users group there, and was quite

which lug?  There's a few dozen big ones out there.

IISc had a sunsite mirror, as well as some other distro mirrors - but
this is as of years back.  sunsite.serc.iisc.ernet.in is still up and
running but with a rather old looking wu-ftpd 2.6.1(1), that was the
default for I think RH 6.2 - and for example "dir" gives me a 421
service not available error.

Doubt if the mirror is being maintained now - it it is not, it'd
probably be best to take it offline till the box is patched .. versions
upto 2.6.2 (the latest) have their fair share of security holes.

vasudevan rk wrote:
> Hi Luggies!
>      Can anyone suggest me where to get REMOTE servers(LINUX) preferably
> RedHat Enterprise Linux - 4.0 and CentOS - 4.4 from any good data
> centers in
> US like theplanet.com, softlayer.com, ..etc..

Theplanet / ev1 is not bad and neither is rackspace if you want
dirtcheap colocation with cpanel boxes etc.

Softlayer (formed by a bunch of ex theplanet execs) has significant spam
problems - lots of spammers used to be hosted there, better situation
now but ..

Other places like XO (http://www.xo.com), Pair (http://www.pair.com) - a
bit costlier but well worth the money.

Subject: [Ilugc] How is linux secure
In-Reply-To: <727912d50703061611w5d900991w311499a510307a4d@mail.gmail.com>

On 3/7/07, Vinayak Mahadevan <vinayak.mahadevan@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Dear Ilugies
>
> Around 2 days back I was trying to convice my marketing director about
> switching over to linux for certain machines in my company. In the course
> of
> the discussion he asked a seemingly simple question "as to how is linux
> more
> secure than windows even though the source code of linux is available
> whereas the source code for windows is not available". Can anybody help me
> to answer this question.
>
>
The first and foremost of security is the least dependency on the software
vendor itself. one example i heard from fsf friends. a bangalore based
company invested some lakhs to develop a software to suit their needs. they
approached a software developer and got it designed and developed to suit
their needs. they failed to get the source code or were ignorant of that.
they next year when they turned back for enhancement the developer could not
be found out. had they been aware of the importance of source code and power
this would have been a minimal loss.

as long as relationship goes smooth with the software vendor its honey. when
it starts itching, source code does matter a lot. :-)

On 07-Mar-07, at 5:41 AM, Vinayak Mahadevan wrote:

> the discussion he asked a seemingly simple question "as to how is  
> linux more
> secure than windows even though the source code of linux is available
> whereas the source code for windows is not available".

imagine two huge buildings. he wants to rent one for an office. Both  
are in a place where earthquakes and terrorist acts are common. For  
one, he is given a complete building plan, clearly marking all the  
exits and entrances and the complete wiring etc of the building  
showing all maintainence passageways, ducts etc. For the other, he is  
told that no plans are available or can be shown because terrorists  
might get access to them - but since the details of the building are  
top secret, no terrorist can misuse the details. Regarding wiring and  
things, they say, we cannot give you the details, but give us the  
ends of the wires and we will connect them for you - same for exhaust  
pipes etc etc. Which building will he choose?

From manokaran at gmail.com  Wed Mar  7 09:33:37 2007
From: manokaran at gmail.com (Mano)
Date: Wed Mar  7 09:34:13 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] How is linux secure
In-Reply-To: <727912d50703061611w5d900991w311499a510307a4d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <727912d50703061611w5d900991w311499a510307a4d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <7bf1bec50703062003x2940c2feqd39cba6f11146950@mail.gmail.com>

On 3/7/07, Vinayak Mahadevan <vinayak.mahadevan@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Around 2 days back I was trying to convice my marketing director about
> switching over to linux for certain machines in my company. In the course
> of
> the discussion he asked a seemingly simple question "as to how is linux
> more
> secure than windows even though the source code of linux is available
> whereas the source code for windows is not available". Can anybody help me
> to answer this question.
>

Software intrinsically is a complex beast. When the source code is
available, people who have no ulterior motives can point out defects and
maybe even fix it themselves. Though there is no money in doing this bug
detecting and fixing, the recognition and the accompanying prestige is heady
stuff for many. More so for the brighter ones! And because of this a lot of
bright ones pore over open source applications (the popular ones) looking
for bugs. So, even before (or atleast as soon as) the bad guys can get to
exploiting it, the bugs get detected and fixed.

In  contrast, the number of people who get to look at the source code of a
closed source app - the employees of the company which builds it - is
limited.... even for someone as big as Microsoft! And the motivations of
these employees are not always prestige and recognition! Compounding this
situation is the fact that a hell a lot of information can be gleaned just
by black box testing an application. And it is usually the bad guys who
indulge in these stuff. Because good people who indulge in such stuff can be
penalized for breaking the licensing terms! So, it is always the bad guys
who know of a defect in a closed source tool ..... much much before even the
company which built it!

QED

Hope this helps in convincing your boss :-)

regds,
mano

-- 
Software is like a parachute, its safer when it is open
    -Anon

From anandsaha at gmail.com  Wed Mar  7 12:59:51 2007
From: anandsaha at gmail.com (Anand Saha)

Subject: [Ilugc] How is linux secure
In-Reply-To: <727912d50703062210q7fee9887w694d038dfc96098d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <727912d50703062210q7fee9887w694d038dfc96098d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <154eca020703062329xd8322e5t6a82f4fca4e2dc18@mail.gmail.com>

On 3/6/07, Vinayak Mahadevan <vinayak.mahadevan@gmail.com> wrote:
> Thanks a lot for the clarifications. I think now I can go and convince my
> boss about shifting to linux and saving money.

Take a gun with you.

Some points which might help you in convincing him:
- Avoiding "Vendor Lockin"
- Return on Investment, Total Cost of Ownership
- Availability of Support (and the cost factor)
- Interoperability : high in FOSS
- Stability of the software (Industrial strength software e.g. for networks)

Now, you might need numbers, for which you will need to do some
googling on these.

However, there are certain other practical factors which must be taken
into acount. Availability of an experienced person to administer the
installations at your end, for example (yes, you might learn it on job
as well :) Next, the learning factor. You might find it desirable for
your Accounts and Administration department to use Linux desktop with
Open Office, but there should be eagerness on their side as well. Things
can be forced upon, as a management decision, but might not turn up well
accepted. All you will get is cribbing remarks (believe me, i have experienced
this!)

You need to be doubly careful if your installations has anything to do
with your clients. SLA, Client's policies etc. will come in the way, if at all.

saha

install are expensive. Training and migration - again expensive.  
Installation for doze is pretty cheap because manpower is easily  
available, and migration is not an issue at all since most people are  
familiar with it.

So, need to mention to the marketing folks about:

* GPG-signed binary packages in distro repositories or
in free/open source package hosting websites.

* Only developers get access to commit to CVS
repository, which is again reviewed by other
developers, and people who do testing.

* All changes/commits to CVS updated in project logs,
so everyone gets to know what is *happening*.

From joe_steeve at gmx.net  Thu Mar  8 12:54:14 2007
From: joe_steeve at gmx.net (Joe Steeve)
Date: Thu Mar  8 12:55:19 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Hard Disk Bad Sectors
In-Reply-To: <727912d50703072316x13f5fd4fo53dd754f253a7406@mail.gmail.com>
References: <727912d50703072316x13f5fd4fo53dd754f253a7406@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <45EFBA1E.1030702@gmx.net>


Hello.,

Vinayak Mahadevan wrote:
> I have a mail server running FC5 in my company. The hard disk
> capacity is 160 GB. It has developed 1 bad sector. Is it safe to run
> the mail server with that hard disk or is it better to change the
> hard disk.

Keep watching periodically to see if the number of bad sectors increase.
If they keep increasing., there is a hardware problem with the drive. If
so., the best would be to change the drive.

Suggestion: You can run software raid using two 160GB hard-drives. It is
pretty easy to setup on gnu/linux with 'mdadm'. It'll save a lot of
trouble for you in the longer run, and is not very expensive. Just costs
another hard-drive.

-- 
.o. I'm a Free man. I use GNU/Linux.
..o
ooo [W] http://www.joesteeve.org/

Dear Ilugies
In my company I have got a FC5 box working as the linux email server. The
main work this does is collect mails from an external mail server and then
distributes the mail locally. Mails which are generated within the company
and which are addressed to the company domain are distributed locally. What
I would like to know is that suppose a person with the id
a...<http://groups.google.co.in/groups/unlock?msg=52042eecd14526e1&hl=en&_done=/group/comp.mail.sendmail/browse_thread/thread/554960939f773714/52042eecd14526e1%3Fhl%3Den>
@xxxx.com(this id exists in the local mail server) sends a mail to a person
with id x...<http://groups.google.co.in/groups/unlock?msg=52042eecd14526e1&hl=en&_done=/group/comp.mail.sendmail/browse_thread/thread/554960939f773714/52042eecd14526e1%3Fhl%3Den>
@xxxx.com(this id does not exist in the local mail server but exists in the
external mail server) is there any way to force sendmail to try sending it
to the external mail server. Right now what is happening is that it bounces
back
saying user not found.
Thanks and Regards
Vinayak

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Thu Mar  8 18:16:58 2007
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Thu Mar  8 18:18:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Sendmail Configuration
In-Reply-To: <727912d50703080347w19d33f43w117861c5be7be422@mail.gmail.com>
References: <727912d50703080347w19d33f43w117861c5be7be422@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <45F005C2.7020907@frodo.hserus.net>

Google for "mailhub configuration"

Easiest way is to create "madras.yourdomain.com" - and if you have a
public, static IP (which you can get from any dsl provider), set that up
with MX and A records for your static IP

madras.yourdomain.com.	IN	MX	10	madras.yourdomain.com.
			IN	A	your.static.ip

Then you'd have to have some way of syncing the userdb across the place
- and defining whether user@yourdomain.com is local (that is his account
is an alias to his madras.yourdomain.com account) or external.

There should be reasonable cookbook configs for whichever mailserver
you're running - I would recommend a common userdb across the actual
mailserver and the local one

Please do not mind, but let me give you my frank opinion, since you
persist.

Difference between 'r u ppl' and "are you people": one is a set of
characters used as shorthand for SMSing, while the other is a phrase
which makes complete sense to anyone with a decent command over the
English language.

Personally, yes, I do NOT want to understand "r u...", partly because
I take time to compose complete words and expect others on the list to
do the same. Most others do.

understand or you don't want to understand?

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Fri Mar  9 06:18:21 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Fri Mar  9 06:08:37 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] configure doesn't find the installed libraries
In-Reply-To: <526626.18362.qm@web25405.mail.ukl.yahoo.com>
References: <526626.18362.qm@web25405.mail.ukl.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20070309004821.GB5187@localhost>

On Thu, Mar 08, 2007 at 10:11:14PM +0000, Vignesh wrote:
> Now, when I run configure for application a, the
> configure complains "x not found.  x is a must if you
> need to install a".  I could see the libraries present
> in /usr/local/lib folder, but configure doesn't seem
> to be recognizing it.

You must notice that /usr/local/lib contains the binary shared
objects. However, to be able to build your package from source, you
need the headers corresponding to these libraries. These headers are
ususally present in a "dev" or "devel" package for that software.

For example, you might have the GTK+ ".so" files, but without the
GTK+ "devel" package, you will not be able to compile and link GTK+ programs.

> I am trying to install libopenikev2_impl which needs
> libopenikev2.

Have you installed libopenikev2 from source? Do you have the headers?

Kumar

Indian Institute of Technology Madras,
Chennai - 600 036

From goda.abishek at gmail.com  Fri Mar  9 08:55:49 2007
From: goda.abishek at gmail.com (Ingenieur)
Date: Fri Mar  9 08:56:27 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] configure doesn't find the installed libraries
In-Reply-To: <526626.18362.qm@web25405.mail.ukl.yahoo.com>
References: <526626.18362.qm@web25405.mail.ukl.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <70106e0b0703081925m6860d265r2873d12b1e82132a@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 3/9/07, Vignesh <mvikyk@yahoo.co.uk> wrote:
> Hi,
>
> I am trying to install an application a that requires
> libraries x, y, z.
>
> I first compile and install x (and later y and z) in
> /usr/local/lib (default).

Good. If you compiled and installed it, just set the $PKG_CONFIG_PATH
variable to include $LIBRARY_INSTALL_PATH/lib. ie if x was in
/usr/local/x/ then do export
PKG_CONFIG_PATH=$PKG_CONFIG_PATH:/usr/local/x/lib. In you case it is
just /usr/local/lib. Do this for every dependant library that you
install. Then compile the final source. It is usually the
<library_name>.pc file that resides in the pkgconfig directory that
sources the library's include details.

Note, if that did not work, try adding /usr/local/lib/pkgconfig to the
variable. I don't quite get the exact variable now!

Hope that helps.
-- 
Regards,

Abishek Goda
http://abishek.wetpaint.com

From solar345 at gmail.com  Fri Mar  9 09:06:13 2007
From: solar345 at gmail.com (Antano Solar)
Date: Fri Mar  9 09:06:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] How is linux secure
In-Reply-To: <727912d50703061611w5d900991w311499a510307a4d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <727912d50703061611w5d900991w311499a510307a4d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <b2600ec40703081936t157e145bi14ebff88cf0405e2@mail.gmail.com>

>
> Around 2 days back I was trying to convice my marketing director about
> switching over to linux for certain machines in my company. In the course of
> the discussion he asked a seemingly simple question "as to how is linux more
> secure than windows even though the source code of linux is available
> whereas the source code for windows is not available". Can anybody help me
> to answer this question.
>
You could probably use the following metaphor.
Say the encryption algorithms all of them are open , but the keys are
the ones private.
But still they are good at keeping the transaction secure.

Similarly , There are two different concepts , data and code.
Security in most sense is how safe the data can be , and that needs
intelligent code , more the number of participants and more trial and
error and more possible commits and development , better the code.Open
source achieves just that :) And explain to him his data will still be
confidential and its not 'open data' :)

as far as i can see, the rules seeking to be enforced are:

1. posting in full english rather than sms-speak
2. putting meaningful subject lines - and not putting subject lines  
from digests which have no meaning
3. avoiding top posting
4. preventing birthday lists and tags and other invitations

can you please explain how these rules are 'axeing freedom'? How can  
you say that 'Rulers' are bullying others? Or are there other  
instances where freedom has been curbed? You should either  
substantiate your allegations or withdraw them. If, on the other  
hand, you feel the mailing list should have no rules at all, you are  
free to campaign for that and if you can convince the list admin, all  
rules may be removed and we can have total 'freedom'. but remember,  
there is a difference between freedom and anarchy.

> >
> > http://www.zdnetindia.com/news/software/stories/172654.html
> >
> > TN orders 40000 desktops with linux ... and Windows starter edition dual
>
> Its a good move. But my question is how many will boot into Linux in a
> dual boot machine?

The reason for using dual boot with Windows starter edition is that it
has many limitations. For example, in Windows starter edition the user
may not open more than 3 windows simultaneously (ex: firefox). Whereas
we all know, the user do not have such limitations in Linux.

As per Umashankar it would be the driving aspect for forcing them to
use Linux! Interesting aspect of this deal is the offer itself:

Desktop without OS: Rs.21800
Desktop with Winxp Starter edition pre loaded: Rs.21800
Desktop with Suse linux enterprise edition: Rs.21800

The ELCOT negotiated for dual boot for Rs.22000. Please refer to
egovindia yahoo group for tons of interesting emails sent by
Umashankar in this context.

http://groups.yahoo.com/group/eGovINDIA/

Which takes me to a deeper question (a recurring one to those who have read

Mano wrote:
  > Pls dont tell me that quanta, emacs, gimp can come anywhere close to
> photoshop, dreamweaver with regard to ease of use!

The point is that the "any question about photoshop, dreamweaver or 
anything proprietary" doesn't come anywhere close to the purpose or 
intention of this mailing list. (exception may be if the OP is asking 
about an FOSS alternative to these softwares).

If you want to post about HTML, CSS, AJAX jobs you are free to do it 
here - but not Photoshop or Dreamweaver. You can say something like 
"Ability to work with HTML,CSS, AJAX and other proprietary tools"

But the OP's post read like "Web Designers with High creativity and 
amazing graphic
design abilities, knowledge of tools like Adobe Photoshop, Illustrator,
Macromedia Dream Weaver, ..." so the more important qualifications being 
mentioned are no where near the interests of this mailing list.

Am afraid the OP is not looking only for an Open Source Web 
Developer/Designer with HTML, CSS, AJAX ?

** Again - this is not a job portal but a Linux User Group's Mailing 
List. Please post relevant job opportunities only.

*** I am not making a rule or trying to be authoritative - just pressing 
the original purpose of this mailing list. If you think am wrong, you 
have the freedom to neglect this mail.

On Thu, 2007-03-08 at 23:17 +0600, Zico wrote:
> nobody said anything about my real problem.. the "bad sector" problem...
> what will i do for that? i check my hard disk with badblocks but it didn`t
> find anything though Norton disk doctor finds the bad sector.
> 
> is there any rule that, i can block my bad sector partition for all the time
> in linux?
> 
> Zico


Zico, People are here to help you for free. The question you asked
initially was "how to configure the bad sector in linux?". Is should
probably be "How do I fix bad sector problems in Linux". And it is
better if you include other information like, what exact error you are
getting, what OS you are using, which partition has bad sectors, etc. 

There are many ways to solve your problem. If you find bad sectors in
root or home partition, then I would recommend you to get into single
user mode, and run fsck. 

http://www.linuxforums.org/forum/redhat-fedora-linux-help/60822-how-enter-single-user-mode-grub.html 
explains about getting into single user mode. 

You can also use a livecd, to boot and run fsck on your hard disc.

Subject: [Ilugc] Resume Download in Apache-httpd
In-Reply-To: <1173455334.2293.0.camel@localhost>
References: <1173350907.45efe9fbe4a6b@secure.symonds.net>
	<1173455334.2293.0.camel@localhost>
Message-ID: <45F1923F.6080600@gmail.com>

Deepan wrote:
> On Thu, 2007-03-08 at 16:18 +0530, vipintm@au-kbc.org wrote:
>   
>> Hi,
>>
>>
>> Does apache-httpd support resume download ?
>> if not, any patch / mod is available to do this?
>>     
>
> I think resume download is a feature of the download manager. I am not
> very sure though. May be someone else can clarify for us :)
Unless the server support HTTP 1.1 fully, the download manager can't do 
anything here. For more info,

http://www.w3.org/Protocols/rfc2616/rfc2616-sec14.html#sec14.35.2
http://support.microsoft.com/kb/229704
http://httpd.apache.org/docs/1.3/misc/known_client_problems.html (see 
the Byterange section.)

I believe since apache 1.3 this feature is supported. If I am right, the 
parallel download by some client use this feature. This you can see in 
popular window only DMs like Flashget, Download accelerator,etc.,

-- Guru Prasath

Date: Sat Mar 10 06:11:35 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] does it matter to artists
In-Reply-To: <7bf1bec50703090553g114bd888r301aa53ddb24c9cd@mail.gmail.com>
References: <7bf1bec50703090553g114bd888r301aa53ddb24c9cd@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <235E8B50-2F7A-4F87-B354-E848C1E126B6@thenilgiris.com>


On 09-Mar-07, at 7:23 PM, Mano wrote:

>> tools like quanta, emacs, gimp, blender etc etc.
>>
>>
> Hair splitting!

nope
>
> Which takes me to a deeper question (a recurring one to those who  
> have read
> my earlier posts): How does it matter to an artist whether the  
> source code
> of the tool he is using is available or not!! Say a painter has  
> access to a
> propreitary concoction that helps achieving superior results easier  
> than
> those for which the formulas are available! Should he forsake the
> opportunity to create superior works of art?

nope. It all depends on the level of the professional. A professional  
needs professional tools. In certain areas foss products do not  
measure up. For example in dtp, scribus is nowhere near pagemaker or  
quark express. So a professional would have to use the latter -  
whether he likes it or not. As long as he pays for it, no problem.  
Similarly, in vector graphics, inkscape is not a patch on corel draw.  
On the other hand, gimp *does* compete with photoshop and  
professionals can use it. Likewise, blender is kick-ass professional  
animation software which can easily compete with the proprietary  
competition. In the mid- nineties, i used to use corel draw,  
pagemaker and photoshop, but had to stop because each of the cost  
around 25K and the business I was doing did not generate the revenue  
for me to keep upgrading - and my competitors were all using  
'free' (as in beer) versions. In this context note that creative dot  
accepts contributions composed using closed software on condition  
that the author has paid for the software

>
> Pls dont tell me that quanta, emacs, gimp can come anywhere close to
> photoshop, dreamweaver with regard to ease of use!

gimp competes favourably with photoshop, but the learning curve is  
steep. Dreamweaver is a piece of sh*t and no self respecting designer  
would use it anyway. Existing foss products cannot yet compete with  
illustrator, coreldraw, pagemaker, quark express. That said, when you  
factor in the cost of these, unless you are a fulltime, well earning  
professional, you *have* to make do with the foss tools. Question -  
how many people in this list, who have used any of the above tools  
have paid for them?

-- 

regards
kg
http://lawgon.livejournal.com
http://nrcfosshelpline.in/web/

It matters, only if it is let to matter.

I would buy a CRY or HelpAge card, If it matters to me as to where the
money goes and whether it helps the helpless. Else I will just buy any
card which pleases my taste (might as well be the CRY or HelpAge card).

> Say a painter has access to a
> propreitary concoction that helps achieving superior results easier than
> those for which the formulas are available! Should he forsake the
> opportunity to create superior works of art?

Should he ? Shouldn't he? The artist in question knows better, who ever it is.

From solar345 at gmail.com  Sat Mar 10 20:39:09 2007
From: solar345 at gmail.com (Antano Solar)
Date: Sat Mar 10 20:39:48 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: ilugc Digest, Vol 34, Issue 23
In-Reply-To: <888e59e70703080221y51bee2bcs4e8b5fe35a47616c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <20070308063002.D16171DB281@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
	<888e59e70703080221y51bee2bcs4e8b5fe35a47616c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <b2600ec40703100709g4805de02qaba13b2e901f3b7a@mail.gmail.com>

On 3/8/07, sanjeev saini <sainisanjeev@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hey does anyone have an idea about how to recover data from a usb pen drive.
> One of my friend has accidentally deleted a file which was very important to
> him. Can someone suggest how to get back the file.
>
> Regards
> ss
>

Depends on the filesystem ,
if its fat32 , try the .trash as somenoe has just said.
even if it is not there , you can possibly recover using recovery
tools like 'undelete' in windows.
In a delete what happens is only the fat entries are deleted , and the
file contents say intact , so even if you recover sometimes you dont
get the right name of the file but you will get the contents.So if the
files are media files its not a problem but if you want a set of files
for a single application , dont even bother trying undelete.
Sophisticated tools take upto an hour to run the whole process for
like 512 mb or 1 gb drive.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sun Mar 11 11:19:50 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Mar 11 11:20:44 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] FLOSS workshop, Osmania University, Hyderabad, March 10,
	2007
Message-ID: <20070311054950.8222.qmail@web50204.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi,

I conducted a "Careers with GNU/Linux and Free
Software" workshop on Saturday, March 10, 2007 at
Osmania University, Hyderabad.

I would like to thank Dr. Atul Negi (Vice-Chairman,
IEEE Hyderabad Section), Dr. Madhav Negi (Chairman,
IEEE Computer Society, Hyderabad Section) for their
support in this workshop.

Thanks to Santosh Arjun (Vice-Chairman, IEEE Student
Chapter, Osmania University) for working with me for
more than a month in organizing this workshop.

* This is the first time that I actually "flew" to a
workshop. Indian Airlines [1] flight was delayed by
two hours. The workshop was to start at 10:15, but, I
reached Hyderabad [2] only at 1200 noon. But, was able
to catch up with the sessions: Careers with GNU/Linux,
Free Software, GNU/Linux desktop, Embedded HOWTO,
Alliance VLSI CAD Tools HOWTO
(http://www.shakthimaan.com/downloads.html). 

* The posters made for the workshop are available at:

http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/posters/flyer_workshop.pdf

http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/posters/flyer_workshop_2.pdf

* There were about 180 students from in and around
Hyderabad. There were students who came all the way
from Vijayawada (300 km) by bus, overnight, and I was
elated! 

* Students from other colleges who participated in the
workshop were eager to have similar workshops for
their colleges. I have agreed for the same.

* Was able to meet folks from Free Software
Foundation, Andhra Pradesh Chapter.

* I shall provide the organizers' contacts to NRC-FOSS
(Krishnan, Kenneth, Shrinivasan, Parthan, et. al.).

* I am still awaiting some photos from the students.
Once I get them I shall upload them and provide the
link.

Regards,

SK

[1] Please avoid in future. No refreshments were
served for  passengers waiting in the lounge, due to
the delayed flight. Further delay caused due to
engineering problems.

[2] Hyderabad is a Pretty Hot Place (PHP?).  It was 30
degree celsius, but, felt like 50!

--
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

Suresh Ramasubramanian <linux@frodo.hserus.net> writes:
>> nobody said anything about my real problem.. the "bad sector"
>> problem...  what will i do for that? i check my hard disk with
>> badblocks but it didn`t find anything though Norton disk doctor
>> finds the bad sector.
>
> fsck your partitions after dropping into single user mode
>
> if there's really multiple bad sectors and its because of
> failing hardware .. then you're best advised to get your data
> backed up
>
> replacing the hard disk is the only cure, beyond a point

Specifically you can use 'fsck -c' to invoke the badblocks program
to do a non-destructive test. 

But you'll have to keep watching for occassional errors to see if
the badblocks count is growing. I dont know whether these guys at
ritchie street are informed enough to replace a hard-disk with
bad-sectors under warranty. Try your luck.

Anurag wrote:
>> by the way, what for is "xchm" used?
> 
> for viewing windows compiled html type html files i guess.

A lot of pirated ebooks come as .chm files. It is *Microsoft Compressed 
HTML Help Files*. It is basically used to create Help files in MS 
Windows. But, have seen a lot of pirated ebook copies of books being 
available in the Internet in this format.

just posting a URL, where the content of the url pointed to is  
perfectly understood is not conducive to discussion. Simply posting  
URLs should be frowned upon. When posting a URL, one must also put a  
few words as to why the OP thinks it is interesting, or why he posted  
it. Of course everyone has broadband nowadays, so bandwidth is not  
wasted, but time is wasted clicking something that may or may not be  
of interest.

	<e3dcb5360703111957r9886d91x6fc78d8d9fcb7c5@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <45F4DA03.5070207@frodo.hserus.net>

First - I'm tamilian but my tamil has a weird accent (start with a
tirunelveli accent and then layer on the fact that I've spent less than
4 years of my life in madras), I can barely read bus and shop signs in
tamil, certainly can't read long paragraphs in newspapers, or
handwritten tamil letters from my late grandmother back when she was
alive, etc without a lot of effort. Tamil newspapers not worth that
effort - grandmothers letters certainly.

I was reading an excellent english translation of Kalki's Ponniyin
Selvan (published by Macmillan India, trans by CV Karthik Narayanan) and
the introduction to it had these facts .. Kalki was very well regarded
as a tamil scholar (by people like Thiru Vi Ka and others), and a
champion of tamil in music (which brought him into contact with MS and
Sadasivam of course, much to the benefit of music) ..

However he was in favor of modernizing tamil substantially, and was
completely against the highly sanskritized and formal tamil used by some
scholars (samples of such writing can be found in for example
"devotional" magazines, and the inhouse journals of the sringeri /
kanchi math, etc).  He was also completely against "sentamizh" which
steadfastly looked for pure tamil words "untainted" by sanskrit - even
referred to it as "kodunthamizh" - tortured tamil .. something that
various tamil purists, including Thiru Vi Ka - completely disagreed
with, even while they respected Kalki.  In fact Kalki's novels
modernized tamil literature the way that Bharathiar did Tamil poetry.

But that was the 30s and 40s.  The world has come a long way since then,
and so has "modern" tamil as spoken by the common man.

Tamil needs several degrees more modernization, including freely
adapting words from English for things like computing terms. After all,
English grew to where it is now by freely borrowing from every single
language under the sun (start with old anglo saxon, germanic and celtic
languages, add french and latin under the normans, layer on several
expressions from former british colonies - all the way from australia
and the USA to India / china / the middle east and persia, etc)

That is why english, as a language, is alive and constantly evolving.
And why the oxford english dictionary has thousands of words in it that
are derived from hindi, tamil, telugu, persian etc.

Please dont stick to chenthamizh, or doordarshan style tamil. Dont coin
entirely new tamil words, or adapt old tamil words like kanini (a
"counter" right?) for computer

?. ???? ??????? wrote:
> kanini is almost now put into pratice or atleast understandable as
> computer.. a stage has evolved where kanini is now identified as computer..
> the desirable sitution would be a time where equlivalent terminology exists
> and easily understandable for an individual in both languages.. just like
> kathirikkai for brinjal etc.,
> 
> say for example, i would certainly not force ??????? to be used for network
> at this point of time but will definitely choose to simultaneously mention
> both of them.. so that in course of time it evolves as a replacement of
> network and easily used understandable, synonymous to network...  just like
> ????? has evolved and easily identified with computer .

Dear All,

I am extremely happy to announce bioubuntu-0.1 based on Ubuntu Edgy Eft (6.10) 
which is a live GNU/Linux cd with 30 bioinformatics packages covering 
pairwise alignment, multiple alignment, phylogeny and other miscellaneous. 
It is a customized ubuntu live distribution updated to bugfixes which aims
to introduce linux to biology/bioinformatics community thereby bring the 
power and ease  of ubuntu to biologists/bioinformaticians/computational biologists. 

we would shorty start with packaging other bioinformatics tools and
make them available in future versions of the bioubuntu. This BioUbuntu CD was
released at a workshop on " Trends in  Systems Biology and  Bioinformatics " 
 held at madurai kamaraj university (6-8 march 2007) funded by 
Department of Biotechnology, Government of India.

for iso image, photos and presentations pls visit:

http://bicmku.in:8082/bioubuntu

suggestions: bioubuntu-team@mrna.tn.nic.in

regards,
KM

In-Reply-To: <2d0135b0703080936p53025f3fq7e160f13b9d90779@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070312145435.19466.qmail@web50807.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

hello

I used have a few troubles with this myself , tho on a diffferent distro. Till i learnt that several companies like intex do not provide original RTL chipsets. I think both the C and D in RTL LAN adapters use 8139too module, if i am correct.
Cards from Compex have no trouble like this to the best of my knowledge.

regards
devafree

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Mon Mar 12 21:42:26 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Mon Mar 12 22:25:16 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: GUI in Linux
In-Reply-To: <c021e3c90703120735j29b3f9fcua33db216956ae28e@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070312161227.8089.qmail@web50207.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Ambuj Thacker <ambuj.mbp@gmail.com> wrote:
> systems.I have tried to minimize the kernel size
> many times but have failed
> drastically.

What did you try? 

What is your hardware?

Which Linux kernel version?

> I want to know if there is any special
> kernel for Linux?

Linux _is_ the kernel.

> I am
> trying to have only thr required driver for the
> embeded system.

A driver interacts with hardware and the kernel
subsystems. So, you will require the essential kernel
subsystems to exist for the driver to work.

For example, if you want to use USB controller drivers
(ohci_hcd or ehci_hcd or uhci_hcd), you need the USB
subsystem (usbcore) support enabled in the Linux
kernel.

SK

Shakthi Kannan

Not sounding sarcastic or authoritative.. lets hide "Chennai" and consider.

[1] I am happy that your English is good such that we (or at least I) 
could understand what you meant to say. If you are not good in English 
and you do know how to type in local language, then which language would 
you have preferred to ask the question ? (Not bringing in the argument 
that still you could have asked the question in English, that only 
mistakes make a man perfect. But people has to understand what one means 
to correct his mistakes correctly ;-) )

[2] If you don't know Tamil but only Hindi, then you can very well ask 
your question in Hindi. Am sure that there are quite a number of people 
who can understand Hindi, reply you back or at least (as I did a few 
days ago) translate your post to English.

[3] The OP's post was about assistance and contribution to Tamil 
translation for KDE and hence it is not of much problem of the OP to 
convey it in Tamil. :)

Yes. I also dont have any other option too. Nowadays my delete button
is more frequently used on this list. And more fiery are the attitudes
of some people. I can be specific on a lot of "specific" issues but in
the interest of the list I am not listing them down. Also tamil is
fine but _as long as_ there is a translation of whatever is conveyed
following it. People would say that I am not the one to decide and
some such, but I am rising a voice of opinion for quite a lot of
people.

find faults in the question than trying to answer them. Not a good
sign at all. Yes, you can request them to follow List guidelines but
not comment in such a way to start a flamy thread with a "Was Re: blah
bha".

Hope this is taken in good spirit.

From ambuj.mbp at gmail.com  Wed Mar 14 16:25:04 2007
From: ambuj.mbp at gmail.com (Ambuj Thacker)
Date: Wed Mar 14 16:25:44 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] GUI in Linux
Message-ID: <c021e3c90703140355o55682dcahf1fc97d8daf6dcce@mail.gmail.com>

I tried to make the kernel size running on my P.C as small as
possible.Myhardware configuration is
2.4 intel Celeron,Intel 845 chipset (from GIGABYTE),Sony CDROM,80GB ATA
IDE,samsung keyborad.One among thousands of step that I tried was to remove
all the unnecessary drivers.

For this in menuconfig I selected device driver and did the following
changes:

1.In old CDrom drivers: I removed all drivers except sony drivers and
support for non-SCSI IDE cdroms.

2.In block devices I checked on Parallel port IDE drivers.

3.In ATA/ATAPI i checked only IDE/ATA2 disk support.

4.Checked all the SCSI drivers.

5.Removed all old CDROM drivers.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Mar 14 17:30:09 2007

Subject: [Ilugc] GUI in Linux

On Wed, 14 Mar 2007, Ambuj Thacker wrote:

> Is there any special version of Linux for embeded systems?? Where
> can I find information on them??

No. Expect for arch specific sessions, other core kernel part is same
for all the system. In the embedded system, you may need board
specific driver, that is not the part the kernel source, it may be
supplied with Board Support Package(BSP).

For more info: Visit uclinux, mips-linux, arm-linux, ppc-linux,  
project sites.

Bye :)

Bharathi S

From luv2musik at yahoo.com  Wed Mar 14 19:49:48 2007
From: luv2musik at yahoo.com (rajib dutta)
Date: Wed Mar 14 19:50:41 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] GUI in Linux
Message-ID: <20070314141948.63098.qmail@web52018.mail.yahoo.com>

Yes there is an embedded Linux available....

?Clinux (MicroControllerLinux) is a derivative of the Linux kernel for microcontrollers (?Cs, embedded systems) without a memory management unit (MMU).

Since there is npo MMU present there is no concept of address spaces (and further 'Copy on Write')

uClinux was originally derived from version 2.0.38 (1996) of the Linux kernel, it now has ports based on Linux 2.4.0+ and Linux 2.6.

The embedded os has support for many architectures, and forms the basis of many products, like network routers, security cameras, DVD or MP3 players, VoIP phone or Gateways, scanners, and card readers.


you can get more information in the following URLs:-
http://www.uclinux.org/
http://www.uclinux.com/

Rajib

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Wed Mar 14 20:34:06 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)

Message-ID: <20070314150406.20528.qmail@web50207.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Ambuj Thacker <ambuj.mbp@gmail.com> wrote:
> 7.Didnt touch IEEE1394, MPT device and I20 device
>
> P.S. I dont have any knowledge about the devices in
> point-7.

IEEE 1394 is firewire [1] port for real-time data used
with camcorders.

MPT is a Fusion MPT [2] (Message Passing Technology)
from LSI that provides a SCSI host initiator.

I20 [3] is Intelligent Input/Output (I20)
architecture, that allows you to split the
functionality of hardware drivers.

For more details on specific options, you can check
the "Help" link when you do "make menuconfig". For 2.4
Linux kernels, it is present in the Config.in file in
the kernel sources, and for 2.6 kernels, it is present
in the Kconfig file in the kernel sources.

SK

[1] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FireWire

[2]
http://www.lsi.com/insight_center/tech_trends/advanced_architectures/fusionmpt/index.html

[3] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I2O

--
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From mail-lists at karan.org  Wed Mar 14 23:00:34 2007
From: mail-lists at karan.org (Karanbir Singh)
Date: Wed Mar 14 23:02:21 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Doubt with kickstart file..
In-Reply-To: <276770.59391.qm@web50201.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
References: <276770.59391.qm@web50201.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <45F8313A.6050701@karan.org>

Shakthi Kannan wrote:
>> there is no repodata on rh9. 
> For Anaconda? I thought anaconda expects a repodata
> directory in the root of the repository. 
> 
> repodata in:
> http://rh-mirror.linux.iastate.edu/fedoralegacy/redhat/9/os/i386/

look at the isos' for rh9 - you will not find anything like that in there.

that url you are pointing at is only a repo of package made available on 
the net by fedora legacy to satisfy depends for other packages they were 
helping with, not always a part of the core distro. Its not an 
installable tree.

>> the logic for what ?
> 
> unmounting the first CD, ejecting it.

I dont think you need to do that at all. There should be no real need 
for user interaction at install time. The moment you enforce a need to 
ask for user input, you break the idea of automated installs. And you 
loose the ability to install using other media eg. what about users who 
want to install from a http or nfs hosted tree ?

Any user interactive installer options should be handled as modules for 
firstboot, that is run immediately after the first time the machine 
boots, post-install.

If you dont need any user feedback at all, and the kickstart is smart 
enough to make decisions required, then the extra rpms should be 
included in the install media, and the ks.cfg file should be scripted to 
use ( outside the chroot ) /mnt/source/<path to rpms>/

- KB

-- 
Karanbir Singh : http://www.karan.org/ : 2522219@icq

From sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in  Thu Mar 15 10:43:32 2007
From: sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in (P.Sriram)
Date: Thu Mar 15 10:44:35 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Doubt with kickstart file..
References: <45F7EB6C.5030708@midascomm.com>
Message-ID: <loom.20070315T060415-255@post.gmane.org>

Sivaram <sivaramsk@...> writes:
> Actually I want to modify the kickstart file, so that in the post 
> installation it will unmount the last installation cd and eject it, ask 
> for another custom cd(similar to how the anaconda handles ejecting the 
> 1st cd and asks the 2nd cd), which will install some software and then 
> system will reboot.
> 
> Is this possible to do? any pointers??
> 

yeah, you have got many replies, but the answers seemed a bit peripheral to me.
here is a cut and paste from my ks.cfg that i used for rhl8.

%post
#turn on ntpd
/sbin/chkconfig --level 345 ntpd on 
#local software installation
#make temp directory
mkdir /mnt/temp
#nfs mount local software tree
mount dcfserver:/home/rhl8 /mnt/temp
cd /mnt/temp/updates
#update all packages using freshen option
rpm -Fvh *rpm
#update kernel using install option
cd kern
rpm -ivh kern*
#delete old kernel
rpm -e kernel-2.4.18-14
#copy local config files
cd ../files
cp -f resolv.conf /etc/resolv.conf
cp -f ntp.conf /etc/ntp.conf
#install local software
cd ../../extras
rpm -Uvh *
#all done, cleanup
cd /mnt
umount /mnt/temp
rmdir temp
#z end

From vaidhy at loonys.net  Thu Mar 15 12:28:41 2007
From: vaidhy at loonys.net (Vaidhy)
Date: Thu Mar 15 12:29:18 2007
Subject: Way OT - Re: [Ilugc] correct english correct tamil [was
	FLOSSworkshop, Osmania University, Hyderabad, March 10, 2007]
In-Reply-To: <C1F024B2AFA0CE4CB8E93810BD9CAA5402AA9327@xmb-blr-414.apac.cisco.com>
References: <1207559B-0808-4A1E-89A1-69787D4C6466@thenilgiris.com>
	<C1F024B2AFA0CE4CB8E93810BD9CAA5402AA9327@xmb-blr-414.apac.cisco.com>
Message-ID: <e001dc80703142358p366f9eefx72104f56058f008@mail.gmail.com>

One of the basic requirements of language is not whether a concept can be
expressed, but how easy is it express the concept and whether we can think
anf talk in it..  Almost all the suggestions given here would be unpalatable
to a common man.. Why are we so set on a literal translation of a engilsh
term into tamil without thinking about how to express the concept in tamil?

Device = Karuvi
Driver = Iyyaki
Software = menporul (in fact, soft = men, ware = porul)

<rant>
I still remember the translation from Sri, where the simple concepts have
such a convluted wording in Tamil that it is close to unusable. I do not
intend to demean the effort of translating things to Tamil, but the effort
should be aimed at having the man on the street be understand it.
</rant>

Having gotten that off the chest, I realized that the confusion occurs
because the term became popular in another language first. Well, maybe when
we invent things first, we will give it a tamil name and make others
translate it into their language.

Cheers,
Vaidhy

On 3/15/07, Ambuj Thacker <ambuj.mbp@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hello,
>      Thankyou every one for the details.It will take me few days to go
> through all of the inputs.I didnt know about small Linux,will see that too.

What you need is Linux-Tiny kernel patches.
http://itmaze.com.au/articles/linux-tiny/

uCLinux is for arch's with no MMU. The small-footprint distro's are
good but I doubt they have kernel optimizations for size-reduction.

Look at the Linux-Tiny FAQ provided above. Get a kernel from
kernel.org and apply the tiny-patches to it. The last time I looked at
it, you could get a MMU-based kernel with TCP/IP for around 500KB.

I looked at it a long time back(1 year ago), things would have changed
now and you might need to do a bit of reading.

-Toufeeq
-- 
blog @ http://www.toufeeq.net

From: toufeeqh at gmail.com (Toufeeq Hussain)

Subject: [Ilugc] problem with keyboard
In-Reply-To: <848e2ea10703150620h6b953b93j7a70ccab4007b6a6@mail.gmail.com>
References: <848e2ea10703150620h6b953b93j7a70ccab4007b6a6@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <c293dd340703150708q38322c5bs698aa73ef8868acc@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 3/15/07, suthan <83sutha@gmail.com> wrote:
> i am using a hcl laptop(ax2021).the problem i am facing is i dont get the
> pipe character while i type it. instaed the # symbol is displayed.the
> org.conf file says that the keyboard is 105 key model. but mine is 86 key
> model. i edited the file but it didnt work. other keys work well. what
> should i do.i have installed kubuntu. all keys work properly in windows xp.

>From the Konsole run,
'sudo dpkg-reconfigure xserver-xorg'

Choose keyboard Layout as "US" and Keyboard Rules as "xorg".

My xorg.conf has the following options under the keyboard section.

Section "InputDevice"
        Identifier      "Generic Keyboard"
        Driver          "kbd"
        Option          "CoreKeyboard"
        Option          "XkbRules"      "xorg"
        Option          "XkbModel"      "pc104"
        Option          "XkbLayout"     "us"
EndSection

-Toufeeq

blog @ http://www.toufeeq.net

is.

Sripriyan C wrote:
> If someone can give a small write up as to how to make my machine to
> recognize tamizh(both in linux and window env) it would be very useful.
> Its boring to see the unrecognized characters for quite a long time.

As far as I remember, similar question has been asked many times in this 
list and solutions been offered. Please cultivate the habit of checking 
the mailing list archives for similar or related queries before posting 
a question.

Anyway, here is the solution if you want to just view Tamizh -

[1] System --> Settings --> Regional and Language

It will show you a list of languages, check whether you have Tamil in 
it. If not, then "add language" and select Tamil. It will install all 
support needed for Tamil language. When the installation is done, select 
the "Tamil" from list of languages available and add it to the default 
list. If needed, relogin.

[2] If you have problem in Tamil getting properly rendered in FireFox, 
please install 'language-pack-ta' (Am not sure of the package name for 
RH based distros)

* When I googled for 'getting tamil in linux', the 3 & 4 results were my 
own blog. I will again wrtie a new post for enabling Tamil support and 
scim in my blog, though already one exists for installing scim and 
trying in Tamil.


--

From anandsaha at gmail.com  Fri Mar 16 09:18:13 2007
From: anandsaha at gmail.com (Anand Saha)
Date: Fri Mar 16 09:18:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] php problem
In-Reply-To: <69621d830703151512s15e28e0dw88c40b618e2187d1@mail.gmail.com>
References: <69621d830703151512s15e28e0dw88c40b618e2187d1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <154eca020703152048i4e1514fctd8cd9b9f948db6fc@mail.gmail.com>

On 3/16/07, Zico <mailzico@gmail.com> wrote:
> But when the firefox page open, it just remain blank. Nothing like
> "hello"....
> I want to add that, i have installed php5,apache2.0 & mysql.
>
> What is the problem?

hmm ... you get a blank page and no 404 error, means file was found,
but might be that php interpreter didn't work through apache.

Check apache config fie (httpd.conf), that you have the mime correctly set
for .php files. Make sure you have the php module entry in httpd.conf.

LoadModule php5_module        modules/libphp5.so
AddType application/x-httpd-php .php .phtml

The php INSTALL file gives you all steps.

--

Hey Zico,
          Are you able to play audio in other formats (say
wav,ogg,system sounds etc.) If so problem is not with your audio driver.
Maybe you dont have mp3 codecs installed to playback files.
Install gstreamer-plugins-good/bad and ugly with all deps. then you will
be able to play back your audio. Most probably you have just ffmprg
and/or gstreamer-ffmpeg installed now. Xine also maybe having the same
problem. You may hav to install xine-extras to enable playback of mp3
audio and any other proprietary format.

Karthik Ramgopal

Being a tamilian, I have to oppose diluting SenTamizh. :-)
lovingly at least...

Lets remember, Tamil from times immemorial, (Before the stone and sand had
appeared...)...has always been used for poetic purposes.
It was basically suited for poetic and artistic purposes rather than
scientific.

Tamil does not have the depth or the range of sounds as is reqd for this.
Just going through the Hindi/kannada alphabets and this will prove it...
The lang has also not adapted/changed over a long time...
I sometimes get crosseyed just reading school level science books written
tamil.

So it is maybe time..(or was long since pending)..for Tamil++.
I guess Tamil puritans in this group will oppose this...

if you want to host about 10 websites, there are two ways of going  
about it. 'el cheapo', paying around 2-3 k a year for php-mysql- 
cpanel stuff where you only have ftp access. Or going for the real  
thing, a vps hosting with about 10-20 gb of space and root access  
where you can do whatever you want, give your friends shell access,  
use languages like perl, python ruby, web frameworks like django,  
rubyonreals and generally have a ball. tektonic.net, for example,  
gives reliably vps for around 12 k a year. Of course, there is a lot  
of do it your self stuff there - but then thats where the fun comes in.

From shankar1023 at gmail.com  Sat Mar 17 09:51:49 2007
From: shankar1023 at gmail.com (shankar)
Date: Sat Mar 17 09:52:28 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Removing Pen drive safely
In-Reply-To: <BAY116-W9D43C08B0D7AA39FBD48A92700@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY116-W9D43C08B0D7AA39FBD48A92700@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <312b266b0703162121m6137ab38j5715dd3cdfc44bf6@mail.gmail.com>

before eject the pen drive,close all applications the pen drive
used.Thenenter "sync" command will flush the file system
buffers.Then eject the pen drive will automatically power it off.If you were
transfered a bunch of files,this command will really work.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Mar 17 10:53:42 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Mar 17 10:54:38 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Removing Pen drive safely
In-Reply-To: <BAY116-W9D43C08B0D7AA39FBD48A92700@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <101012.98212.qm@web50201.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- "Dinesh ." <udinesh5@hotmail.com> wrote:
> When i want to
> remove my pen drive from my laptop.I do eject it.

After you eject it,

>From the GUI:
Open, say, Nautilus, see if your pen drive icon
vanishes, or says not mounted?

>From the command-line:
Open a terminal and check output of df. See if you
still have an entry for your pen drive, maybe
/media/usbstick or related. If there is no entry, then
it is unmounted and you can remove the device.

SK

--
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

> > buffers.Then eject the pen drive will automatically power it off.If you

> Won't umounting implicitly call sync?

It will... in fact, remounting as read only will sync.. In fact what I
do in my system is remount as ro before unplugging and then pull it
out.. An udev script (I don't use HAL, never needed it..) mounts while
plugging and lazy unmounts it after I unplug the device...

From toufeeqh at gmail.com  Sat Mar 17 17:43:10 2007
From: toufeeqh at gmail.com (Toufeeq Hussain)
Date: Sat Mar 17 17:43:49 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Live Presentation in Linux
In-Reply-To: <200703051520.08664.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>
References: <200703051520.08664.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <c293dd340703170513u41df9d68l27727aae7828e568@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 3/5/07, Shrinivasan T <tshrinivasan@gmail.com> wrote:
> Friends.
>
> I want to teach linux to my remot friends.
> We may be in a same network or may be in  internet.
>
> I need this kind of setup.
>
> They all can connect to my linux and get a window open in their machine.
> I can show anything on that window to all.
> I may show the impress presentations, my shells, my configurations files, my
> settings etc.
> I have to guide them by showing them and i have to talk them in voice, so that
> they can have a very very live session in the internet.
>
> How to do it?

non-FOSS way :
splashcast : You can combine audio/video/RSS-feeds and slideshows into
one meta-file which is hosted at splashcast.
http://splashcastmedia.com/

FOSS-way :
Try flumotion : Where you will setup a streaming server and play a
video file which would be a screencast created using wink(non-foss but
on linux) or istanbul (foss-gstreamer based). www.flumotion.net/ If
you feel flumotion is too much work VLC can also stream a video file.

VNC and X-forwarding have already been suggested so I won't go into
those details. I'm not sure it icecast can do video though.

If you are adventurous try Peercasting. http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peercasting

-Toufeeq
-- 
blog @ http://www.toufeeq.net

> Friends.

> friend's personal, one for a startup etc.
>
> I saw 1and1.com is giving 10GB space for around 3$ per month i.e Rs1800 per
> year.
>
> is that is a good one?
>
> can i use that 10GB space for my 10 websites as 1GB per site?

Based on my experience, syminet.com (aka. symonds.net) is really very
good. They offer wide range of services including enough webspace,
ssh, ftp, mysql, phpmyadmin, pop email accounts, squirrelmail, etc.
Not to mention the quality and support time around. They provide 24x7
support (not just in papers) which is not a common thing in any of
Indian based hosting providers. I've registered around 15 domains with
them in past couple of years and have no reason to look for an
alternative.

But I'm unsure if it will work within your budget. Given the amount of
domains you are going to host, i'm sure you may get a best deal from
them though. Good luck!

> 06:00.0 Ethernet controller: Realtek Semiconductor Co., Ltd.

8139 is a commonly cloned and copied chipset and unless your chipset is
branded realtek, it might have a slightly different implementation .. so
that the standard realtek driver will suck at least slightly

> Mar 18 12:35:09 edgy kernel: [17189842.056000] Disabling IRQ #169 quite

What does cat /proc/interrupts say?  What's irq 169?

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Sun Mar 18 22:42:48 2007
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Sun Mar 18 22:44:40 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Internet Speed Issues in Ubuntu

	<adc51dea0703180950g1d18af2j97986bf2bb0bfd44@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <45FD7310.9090805@frodo.hserus.net>

Aanjhan R wrote:

> It says this
> 169:       1230   IO-APIC-level  yenta, tifm_7xx1, sdhci:slot0,
> sdhci:slot1, sdhci:slot2, wmaster0

That's for your PCMCIA card.  If its crappy .. get rid of it and see if
it works for you.  Nothing wrong with broadcom - 2.6.17 (which you get
in edgy) and up should have pretty decent support for broadcom wifi.

Looks a bit unrelated to your 8139 issues. Just for kicks poke through
the rtl8139 and 8139too module source and see all the sarcastic things
Donald Becker has to say about realtek ..

Make sure you have it on full duplex - if you autonegotiate it it may go
to half duplex, which on an older (10 mbps) hub, can give you real slow
speeds.  Try using a switch instead of a hub and see if that helps.

	srs

From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Mon Mar 19 10:06:30 2007
From: parth.technofreak at gmail.com (Parthan)
Date: Mon Mar 19 10:07:12 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Reg newbie user level presentation
In-Reply-To: <C1F024B2AFA0CE4CB8E93810BD9CAA5402AA9349@xmb-blr-414.apac.cisco.com>
References: <C1F024B2AFA0CE4CB8E93810BD9CAA5402AA9349@xmb-blr-414.apac.cisco.com>
Message-ID: <45FE134E.9090101@gmail.com>

Senthil Sundaram (sensunda) wrote:
> I am looking for a presentation /base material which we can build on
> for the 1 day workshop.
> 
IMHO, please dont bore then with slides and there is no use in showing 
one if the numbers are very limited. Rather start with a basic talk 
about what FOSS and GNU/Linux is and whats all about the philosophy.

Then move to the installation session, do a dual boot with other OS. 
Just show them that the installation is not a problem at all. Just 
mention the two steps they have to take care: [1] partitioning and [2] 
installation of grub.

If feasible have an hands on session of installation, immediately after 
the above. That will increase their confidence of installing and trying 
out Linux.

Once installation is done, use the same system to show them around the 
desktop and what are the applications available by default. If you had 
them have an hands on installation then this session can be really 
interactive and live.

If possible to connect to internet, show them the browsers, mail 
clients, messengers and if they are interested the IRC clients as well.

If they want to play multimedia, show them video and audio players. Tell 
them about prop formats and why they are not supported by default.

If internet is available, show them how to install a software package 
using the distribution's packet manager.

Think this is enough for a good start and they can learn more as they 
become comfortable with their new OS. We do have a presentation which we 
use if for workshops in colleges, but its one and half hour of theory, 
story and philosophy which can not really make people adopt GNU/Linux 
until it is followed by an installation session and hands on feel 
themselves.

-- 
With Regards

Parthan (TechnoFreak)

A Proud GNU/Linux User and Ubuntero

[Web]   https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Parthan
[Blog]  http://technofreakatchennai.wordpress.com

What we do noramally is 

1. we conduct demo day

3. The go home and try
4. they have some problem
5. they ask luggies
6. mostly we dont answer it, but we comment the questions a lot.
7. the newbie gets frustated
8. some of us suggest them to read man pages, tldp.org etc
9. they try it and get more frustated.
10. they giveup
11. they keep telling that linux is tough than windows.

we have to prepare study materials for newbies.
not big howtos, guides.

Without the rc.local entries that does the shutting down and restarting of
the NIC and all other things being equal, even now I have the same problems
I reported in my original thread. With the entries in rc.local I get the
speed normally seen in BSNL broadband (50KBps to 100KBps and sometimes even
250-300KBps).

So, if you are bothered about the semantics of the word you can use
something else but the fact remains that it solves my problem! While it
solves my problem, it obviously is setting something else in motion which
actually is removing the root cause. My post regarding this in the Ubuntu
forum had a response (which I forget now - I think I linked it in my
original post) which might lead you on to the root cause.

try lspci to locate your sound card then
install module for that card using
modprobe "card"
if u can't find ur sound card in lspci then remove ur sound card and boot ur
pc then shutdown and add ur card and then boot it again it detect ur card
now?? follow above steps and configure sound with alsamixer

checks:  ls /dev/dsp*
              ls /dev/mixer*

Subject: [Ilugc] C integration with MySQL
In-Reply-To: <515579.59429.qm@web36813.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <515579.59429.qm@web36813.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <8b665a760703200509hc8305d5yd46efc36c0d08d55@mail.gmail.com>

After installing the mysql client to ur system you can find the
libmysqlclient.so file in /lib/mysql.   Just add that to the  library path
and you ll get it working.
ie., ur compilation command should something like this:
g++ -I /include/mysql -L /lib/mysql  -c<your C file name>
I think this ll help you.

Regards,
Sathya R Narayana.

From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Wed Mar 21 22:23:34 2007
From: parth.technofreak at gmail.com (Parthan)
Date: Wed Mar 21 22:24:20 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Ubuntu:Logging in as root
In-Reply-To: <fa84b3da0703210910o2da4e1f6l2238c2b2f69e77e1@mail.gmail.com>
References: <fa84b3da0703210910o2da4e1f6l2238c2b2f69e77e1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4601630E.5030502@gmail.com>

charanya venkatraman wrote:
> Hello ppl,
> 
>                  I have installed ubuntu 6.0.2 TLS version recently in my
> system.Iam using the Gnome desktop enviroment.
> In gnome there is an option System->Administartion->Users and
> Groups.Inthat,there is an option to change wat administarative tasks
> an user can
> perform. I removed some of the permissions like access to Users and Groups.
> What generally happens when i choose System->Administration->Users and
> Groups is , the root password is asked for and then tasks like
> adduser,delete user can be done.
> Since i removed user access to these i dont get the option
> System->Administration->User and Groups.Now i want it back.How can i do
> tat??It would  be better if i could login as root..Is there anyway to login
> as root without using any options under System->Administration.

In Ubuntu, the first user is given the administrator privileges to do 
installation and other administration work, but this account is not 
equal to a root user account. The root user account is disabled by default.

$ sudo passwrd

If it asks for a password - first, type your current user password
Then it will ask to enter the new Unix password, enter the password for 
'root' and again renter it when it asks.

Now you have the root user account enabled. Login as root and add back 
the administrative privilege to your current user account.

** Remember not to use the root user account frequently. Use 'sudo 
<command>' to execute the command with admin privileges **

HTH :)
-- 
With Regards

Parthan (TechnoFreak)
