> purpose. What I would like to know is that Is there any way where i can
> prevent a person accessing my windows 2000 server and machines which are
> running on the windows network from the linux machine(the browsing
> machine).

Put it on an entirely different network segment and block access to it.
Or put it on a different internet connection altogether


From sbarar at gmail.com  Thu Mar 22 09:40:15 2007
From: sbarar at gmail.com (Sudev Barar)
Date: Thu Mar 22 09:40:55 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Ubuntu:Logging in as root
In-Reply-To: <4601630E.5030502@gmail.com>
References: <fa84b3da0703210910o2da4e1f6l2238c2b2f69e77e1@mail.gmail.com>
	<4601630E.5030502@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <774593a20703212110p6e39ec90se04966fc0592a92f@mail.gmail.com>

On 21/03/07, Parthan <parth.technofreak@gmail.com> wrote:
> charanya venkatraman wrote:
> > System->Administration->User and Groups.Now i want it back.How can i do
> > tat??It would  be better if i could login as root..Is there anyway to login
> > as root without using any options under System->Administration.
>
> In Ubuntu, the first user is given the administrator privileges to do
> installation and other administration work, but this account is not
> equal to a root user account. The root user account is disabled by default.
>
> $ sudo passwrd
>
> If it asks for a password - first, type your current user password
> Then it will ask to enter the new Unix password, enter the password for
> 'root' and again renter it when it asks.

I know this is not what OP asked for but Ubuntu's philosophy of not
having root login is rather neat. You can always drop in to root with
" sudo su - " using your password if you have admin rights. This
method also records who did become root when etc. Mostly it is just a
question of adapting your thinking and running one command at a time
with " sudo comand " or series of commands with " sudo su - "

And you can always add people in to admin group.
-- 
Regards,
Sudev Barar
From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Thu Mar 22 09:58:32 2007
From: parth.technofreak at gmail.com (Parthan)
Date: Thu Mar 22 10:00:28 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Ubuntu:Logging in as root
In-Reply-To: <774593a20703212110p6e39ec90se04966fc0592a92f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <fa84b3da0703210910o2da4e1f6l2238c2b2f69e77e1@mail.gmail.com>	<4601630E.5030502@gmail.com>
	<774593a20703212110p6e39ec90se04966fc0592a92f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <460205F0.8050305@gmail.com>

Sudev Barar wrote:
>> In Ubuntu, the first user is given the administrator privileges to do
>> installation and other administration work, but this account is not
>> equal to a root user account. The root user account is disabled by 
>> default.
>>
>> $ sudo passwrd
>>
>> If it asks for a password - first, type your current user password
>> Then it will ask to enter the new Unix password, enter the password for
>> 'root' and again renter it when it asks.
> 
> I know this is not what OP asked for but Ubuntu's philosophy of not
> having root login is rather neat. You can always drop in to root with
> " sudo su - " using your password if you have admin rights. 

I suppose the OP mentioned that she has removed the 'admin' privilege on 
her account in the 'Manage User and Groups' panel. Hence, she might not 
have administrative privileges to do a "sudo su -", if am not wrong. 
That is why I suggested on enabling the root user account, as she might 
not be having the admin privileges for her current account. So she can 
not add a administrator privilege to any new user account she creates.

I am myself a strong advocate of no-root-user-login, but when she has 
disabled the admin rights on her first account, am afraid there is not 
much way out than enabling the root account and getting back those 
privileges for the user account of hers'. If there is an alternative 
way, other than enabling the root account, I strongly suggest that :)

From tshrinivasan at gmail.com  Thu Mar 22 19:29:26 2007
From: tshrinivasan at gmail.com (Shrinivasan)
Date: Thu Mar 22 19:32:49 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Pakistan Offers Open Source Training Toolkit
Message-ID: <200703221929.27248.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>

Pakistan is the third largest low-cost IT-enabled and offshore business 
processes outsourcing services provider in Asia after India and China. The 
country?s Open Source Resource Center (OSRC), a project of Pakistan?s 
Ministry of Information Technology, has developed and released a FOSS 
resource kit entitled ?OSS Training Toolkit,? originally put together in 
order to facilitate OSRC?s own training workshops in Pakistan. The toolkit 
contains step-by-step manuals in six modules covering various Free and Open 
Source Software applications. All the content is available in printed manual 
form and as OpenDocument (.odt), Portable Document Format (.pdf), and 
Microsoft Word (.doc) files for download.The toolkit covers databases, 
application servers, desktop applications, office productivity suites, 
enterprise resource planning (ERP), and customer relationship management 
(CRM) software, as well as open source desktop applications for both Linux 
and Microsoft Windows. Along with the manuals, the toolkit provides a set of 
CDs that includes two Linux distributions, Ubuntu Linux Desktop and Fedora 
Server, as well as the other applications.

The toolkit?s curriculum has been planned and laid out in such a manner that 
anyone from a basic to novice user can learn and benefit from it. It has been 
released under open source licenses through the OSRC Web site so that 
individuals and organizations interested in migrating from proprietary to 
open source networks can freely download, distribute, use, and modify the 
toolkit and its related CDs. - Fouad Riaz Bajwa

links :
http://www.osrc.org.pk/index.php?option=com_content&task=view&id=29&Itemid=42
http://www.osrc.org.pk/toolkit/oss_toolkit.zip

masquerade_domains =
masquerade_exceptions = root
maximal_queue_lifetime = 1d
message_size_limit = 102400000
mydestination = $myhostname,localhost.$myhostname, localhost.$mydomain,
localhost,$mydomain
mydomain = myserver.com
myhostname = mailsrv.myserver.com
mynetworks = 127.0.0.0/8,192.168.0.0/24
myorigin = $mydomain
newaliases_path = /usr/bin/newaliases.postfix
notify_classes = resource, software, 2bounce, delay, policy, protocol

strict_rfc821_envelopes = no

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Mar 24 18:43:53 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Mar 24 18:44:17 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] GNU Embedded/VLSI workshop, Jaya Engineering College,
	March 24, 2007
Message-ID: <450379.17600.qm@web50212.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi,

I conducted couple of sessions for the ECE, EEE and
EIE department students of Jaya Engineering College,
Thiruninravur, Tamil Nadu, today, Saturday, March 24,
2007.

I would like to thank Prof. Kumaran for his continued
support. Special thanks also to Harish for
coordinating and organizing the event.

I started off with an introduction to Free/Libre/Open
Source Software, taught them examples of Alliance VLSI
CAD tools, and embedded GNU/Linux HOWTO [1]. I gave a
demo of an embedded development kit. 

After the sessions, we had an informal discussion with
the faculty of EEE, EIE.  As such, they are kept
occupied with teaching classes ("theory") round the
clock, correcting assignments, unit tests, exams etc.
I emphasized that this isn't going to take them or the
students any further, in productive "learning", and
compared their work to what their counterparts were
doing in Universities abroad. If time permits, they
said they can work on FLOSS. But, thanks to Prof.
Kumaran's efforts, the team is growing.

After lunch, we had an informal discussion with few
students in the FOSS lab about their final year
project work. Most of them knew only about Java, as
that was what was "prescribed" in the syllabus. But, I
gave them an insight on the different domains that
they could work on, and possibilities available in the
Industry. Their total lack of exposure was obvious,
but, once they hear a lot about FOSS in the industry,
they are quite eager to know more.

The FOSS lab is running Red Hat 9. The systems have
256 MB RAM, so, I asked them to upgrade to a recent
distro ASAP. They also are in the process of moving to
PHP, mysql for their website [2] , which is not
designed or currently maintained. They agreed.

Server has been obtained from our good friends at
deeproot [3], so they can try to setup an internal
portal (PHP, mysql) for intra-department
communication, data handling.

It was here that I met the "Revmakx" [4]. Atleast,
that's what these four students call themselves. They
are awesome PHP, mysql guys. To do classic PHP, mysql
websites for clients (international, and local) at
this age, they are my ideal FOSS students.

The system administrator in the lab wanted few tips on
networking with Red Hat. I showed him how to use scp
to transfer files between two Red Hat systems. He was
so happy! During summer holidays, Prof. Kumaran wants
to do some FOSS camp for the staff. Should be fun, if
you guys can help out, and if you are in town.

I've already been there couple of times, so, didn't
take any photographs.

Sorry for the long e-mail, just wanted to make sure
that I covered everything.

Regards,

SK

[1] Code and presentation examples are here:
http://www.shakthimaan.com/downloads.html

[2] http://www.jec.ac.in/

[3] http://www.deeproot.co.in/

[4] http://www.rentacoder.com/upload_PSC/AuthorPhotos/AUTHOR_PHOTO2006823154255209.jpg

--
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From: aanjhan at gmail.com (Aanjhan R)

Subject: [Ilugc] BMS College of Engineering - Installation and
	Troubleshooting Session
Message-ID: <adc51dea0703241117i147d35e9i8684a0379264f1b0@mail.gmail.com>

Hi All,

Praveen (http://pravi.co.nr) and myself have been working with the BMS
College of Engineering (http://www.bmsce.ac.in/) folks for around 6
months now and things are beginning to show results. Hats Off to the
students!

Today we were there for a Installation and Troubleshooting session.
The session was attended by around 50 - 60 students in one of the CS
Labs. After briefing the FLOSS Philosophy and pros/cons of proprietary
software to (new)students (How FLOSS could help in Knowledge
acquisition) , the installation session began. We had asked the BMS
LUG folks to handle it and they did it quite well. Installed Fedora,
Debian and Ubuntu on around 6 boxes that were offered by the BMS
College Management.

A lot of doubts were cleared in the discusions that followed with
active participation from the students themselves (not only asking
questions but answering questions posted by their peers)

Whats astounding is these events are now being organised by second
year students after some nice work/motivation from the current final
years. They have already quite a few sessions planned up and also a
major Awareness campaign around end of April for Bangalore Colleges.

Also there are now atleast 8 SoC project Applications going out from
this college after some morale boosting sessions which Praveen, Akshay
(BMS Final Year), Srikanth and myself had with these folks a couple of
weeks before.

Happy to see the BMS LUG begining to ROCK!! Keep Rolling mates! And
the end feedback was that the students asked for more such informative
sessions. Nice to hear this!

Pics here: http://www.flickr.com/photos/tuxmaniac/sets/72157600024313523/

OT: BMS College has a Mountaineering Club!!! They do rock climbing,
mini bungee jumping and stuff during the weekends! Surprised me!!

Reggies.
-- 
Aanjhan

Subject: [Ilugc] telnet not working for a user group

Hi,
       I am managing a server in BITS Pilani and am running into a
strange problem. We are using Red Hat Linux 9 (2.4.20-8 smp). The
problem is that one particular user group is able to telnet while the
other is not. The server closes the connection abruptly for them as
soon as they log on. The /var/log/messages file shows the following:

Mar 25 12:48:53 prithvi telnetd[5031]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 15:10:36 prithvi telnetd[7633]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 15:21:07 prithvi telnetd[7843]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 15:22:56 prithvi telnetd[7905]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 15:47:25 prithvi telnetd[8360]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 15:47:30 prithvi telnetd[8361]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 16:54:10 prithvi telnetd[9518]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 17:08:40 prithvi telnetd[9898]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 17:14:57 prithvi telnetd[9991]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 17:35:22 prithvi telnetd[10489]: ttloop: peer died: EOF
Mar 25 18:29:56 prithvi telnetd[11537]: ttloop: peer died: EOF

The other user group however is able to telnet fine. One interesting
point is that all are able to ssh, ftp etc. properly. Further this
problem occurs only if telnet is started via xinetd. If I start
telnetd (telnetd -a off -debug)manually, after stopping xinetd; in
debugging mode, then all are able to telnet fine with no errors
reported. What could be the problem?

The contents of /etc/xinetd.d/telnet file are

# default: on
# description: The telnet server serves telnet sessions; it uses \
#       unencrypted username/password pairs for authentication.
service telnet
{
        disable = no
        flags           = REUSE
        socket_type     = stream
        wait            = no
        user            = root
        server          = /usr/sbin/in.telnetd
        log_on_failure  += USERID
}

The installed packages are as follows
telnet-server-0.17-25.1.legacy
telnet-0.17-25.1.legacy
xinetd-2.3.11-1.9.0

Please help me ASAP as the server is being used for a mission critical
purpose here.

Regards,

Preetish
BITS, Pilani

From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Mon Mar 26 19:24:55 2007
From: parth.technofreak at gmail.com (Parthan)

Subject: [Ilugc] BSNL broadband with linux

Shrinivasan wrote:
> Friends.
> 
> My friend have BSNL 250 plan.
> In windows, he goes to net by clicking "network connections" ... something 
> like that. He gives his username and password and get conneted.
> 
> How to do like this in linux?
> 
> How do u connect?
> 
> where do u give username and password?

from your last post, I assume you are using Ubuntu. Then do open a 
terminal and do "sudo pppoeconf". It will ask you a few questions like 
what is the username, password, etc. Answer them and its done.

You can select auto-connect during booting or use "sudo pon 
dsl-provider" to connect. Use "sudo poff -a" to disconnect.

From aanjhan at gmail.com  Mon Mar 26 19:25:34 2007
From: aanjhan at gmail.com (Aanjhan R)

Subject: [Ilugc] BSNL broadband with linux
In-Reply-To: <200703261913.06216.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>

Hi,

On 3/26/07, Shrinivasan <tshrinivasan@gmail.com> wrote:
> How to do like this in linux?
> How do u connect?
> where do u give username and password?

1. Run pppoeconf as root user
2. The username and password will be asked in the interactive setup
that will follow
3. To connect to the internet type.
             sudo pon dsl-provider

4. Disconnect
              sudo poff  -a

HTH.

Reggies.

From sudharsh at gmail.com  Mon Mar 26 21:15:20 2007
From: sudharsh at gmail.com (Sudharshan S)
Date: Mon Mar 26 21:11:39 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] BSNL broadband with linux

Parthan wrote:
> Shrinivasan wrote:
>> Friends.

>> My friend have BSNL 250 plan.

>> something like that. He gives his username and password and get

>>
>> How do u connect?

>> where do u give username and password?
>
> from your last post, I assume you are using Ubuntu. Then do open a
> terminal and do "sudo pppoeconf". It will ask you a few questions like
> what is the username, password, etc. Answer them and its done.
>
> You can select auto-connect during booting or use "sudo pon
> dsl-provider" to connect. Use "sudo poff -a" to disconnect.
>
Theres another way in which we can connect to the net while the system
initializes its network configuration during the bootup

GUI:
In the Administration > networking..select static
Give the machine ip: 192.168.1.x, where x!=1
Gateway address: 192.168.1.1
and in /etc/resolv.conf add
nameserver 4.2.2.1

Good Ol' Shell:
ifconfig eth0 up 192.168.1.2
route add default gw 192.168.1.1
and entries in the resolv.conf as mentioned above.

To check if it all worked...Open 192.168.1.1 in your browser wherin you
would be greeted by the admin interface of the modem..
Hint: You can enable dhcp from the gateway interface as well

IMO, i feel this is more work but still it doesnt need the pppoeconf
package to be installed, which is the case in some distros..

regards
Sudharshan S

Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
>> You can select auto-connect
> 
> how do you select auto-connect?

When configuring using pppoeconf, it asks a set of questions. One among 
them is "Whether to connect to the internet when you turn on your system 
?" If answered yes, then it connects every time you turn on your computer.

Hello,

On 3/26/07, Srinivasan R <srinivasanr@gmail.com> wrote:
> I did the same for my friend in Airtel. but it doesn't turn on
> automatically.
> even pon doesnt work.

Airtel Broadband is dead simple to configure. No pon , poff nothing.

Just go to System -> Administration -> Networking -> WiredConection
properties -> Select DHCP and re-activate the connection.

Voila you are up and running!

Reggies.

On 3/26/07, Aanjhan R <aanjhan@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Hello,
> Airtel Broadband is dead simple to configure. No pon , poff nothing.
>
> Just go to System -> Administration -> Networking -> WiredConection
> properties -> Select DHCP and re-activate the connection.
>
> Voila you are up and running!
>

So's the case with BSNL!

The h/w box that BSNL provides is not just a modem. It can be configured as
a router that automatically logs on to the BSNL account. It is also a DHCP
server which can dish out network parameters.

Open 192.168.1.1 (the routers ip address) in your browser and type 'admin',
'admin' for username and password, you will see the configuration interface.
You can type in your BSNL account username and password in one of the
screens and have it automatically log on!

I have never done the pon poff stuff in the last 2 years I've been having a
BSNL connection. It just works!

regds,
mano

Eventhough you packetsniffing you will not get the original ip since the
server is acting as a gateway... So you will get the ip address of the
server only not the other peer. For that purpose you have to make a peer to
peer connection to the another end. Example file transfer.

On 3/27/07, Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:
> On 3/27/07, Senthil Murugan <zenmurugan@gmail.com> wrote:
> >
> > So you people mean to say we can connect with two ways
> >
> >    1. Connect using ADSL Router (Connect the phone cable from ADSL
> >    Splitter to ADSL Router (given by BSNL) and then ethernet cable to
> > Machine)
>
>
> Yes.
>
>    2. Use Linux as a ADSL Router itself (Connect Phone cable from ADSL
> >    Splitter to Internal Modem in the M/C) : Is this valid?

There are two ways your modem/router functions, ........... as an
pppoe router or a bridge.

pppoe router :
Configure your computer as just another machine on the same network
that your rouer is in.
If your router ip address is 192.168.1.1(default) , your machine can
have 192.168.1.2 and gateway 192.168.1.1.Ofcourse you can even ask
your router o act as dhcp and avoid this.
User name and password are stord by the router
You need a mechanism for dns . Generally your router can forward dns
for you.else you can run pdnsd or somthing similar and set resolv.conf
approproiately.Your run your own set it as 192.168.1.2(ur comp) router
forwards set it as 192.168.1.1.
All such settings can be changed by going to the page http://192.168.1.1

Bridge:
When you router is in bridge, you dial from the OS to the router  and
supply the user name and password at that time , the router then makes
the connection and something like a bridge is formed between your
computer and the router.i.e two connections are merged into one.

Suggestions : If you have ethernet enabled modem , use the first
method , you get connected when you switch on the modem and there is 0
configuration.If your router is configured for windows or linux you
can simply restart to another OS and its bound to work , ofcourse  you
must set the same ip range.
If you just have a USB connection , go for the second method as thats
the only option.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Tue Mar 27 19:02:37 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Tue Mar 27 19:03:10 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] BSNL broadband with linux
In-Reply-To: <b2600ec40703270332l5afd9542x3313b764c9f6684f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <615164.55583.qm@web50208.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Antano Solar <solar345@gmail.com> wrote:
> Bridge:
> When you router is in bridge, 

Router and bridge are different. Don't mix and match.

The Huawei MT841 provided by BSNL can be operated in
bridge mode as follows:

Login to the web interface of the box, go to
Basic->Connections.

Remove any existing PVC-6 entry. 

Create a new "Bridge" entry with VPI set to 0, and VCI
set to 35. Check on "LLC" for Encap. Click "Apply".
Click "Save All". 

After the box reboots, you can connect any PC to the
ethernet port of the bridge, and use pppoeconf on the
PC to dial, and connect to the ISP.

SK

Shakthi Kannan

again as root.

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: C integratinon with mysql
In-Reply-To: <263376.81580.qm@web36815.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

On Tue, 2007-03-20 at 21:44 -0700, Amit Dey wrote:
> i could not find the folder /lib/mysql
>    
>   I am having a lot of trouble finding the download link for mysqlclient.
>    
>   Can you guys tell me where i could download it.
> 
> 

This command should tell you where you share object file is. 
$locate libmysqlclient.so 

Once you find the folder which has libmysqlclient.so, then 
$g++ -I /include/mysql -L <folder containing libmysqlclient.so>  -c<your
C file name>


If you do not have libmysqlclient.so, then you need to install mysql
package. 
"$yum install mysql"  should help

> This command should tell you where you share object file is.
> $locate libmysqlclient.so
>
> Once you find the folder which has libmysqlclient.so, then
> $g++ -I /include/mysql -L <folder containing libmysqlclient.so>  -c<your
> C file name>

>
> If you do not have libmysqlclient.so, then you need to install mysql
> package.
> "$yum install mysql"  should help
>
>
The /usr/include/mysql  files and libmysqlclient.so  comes with mysql-devel
rpm  (in fedora).  You can check if the package is installed using:
rpm -q mysql-devel

So, the above g++ command would become :
g++ -I/usr/include/mysql -lmysqlclient     ....  .

Regards,
Nived

From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Thu Mar 29 10:08:18 2007
From: parth.technofreak at gmail.com (Parthan)
Date: Thu Mar 29 10:09:56 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Perl Script Execution Error
In-Reply-To: <733535.14988.qm@web7914.mail.in.yahoo.com>
References: <733535.14988.qm@web7914.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <460B42BA.60708@gmail.com>

Raman.P wrote:
> --- ramkumar lakshminarayanan <rajaramcomputers@hotmail.com> wrote:
>>    2. I tried the perl script as follows
>>     
>>    www.rajaramsystems.com/scgi-bin/mytest.pl
>>     
>>    3. I have 777 permission for both the file and the folder.
>>     
>>    But I am getting the following error.
>>    The server encountered an internal error or misconfiguration and
>> was
>>    unable to complete your request.
>>     
>>    Can I anyone point out the mistake of me
> 
> Look at the webserver error log. Actual cause for the error will be
> there.

[1] What does /va/log/apache(or httpd)/error.log say ?

[2] Where have you kept this file ?

[3] Have you given the permission in your httpd.conf or apache.conf to 
execute CGI perl files ?

[4] Never give 777 permission, use 755.

[5] Internal server error also occurs due to problem in the script. 
Error message in the logs is what we need to see first.

[6] Do you have mod_perl installed ?

-- 
With Regards

Parthan (TechnoFreak)

From anoopjohn at gmail.com  Thu Mar 29 12:25:56 2007
From: anoopjohn at gmail.com (Anoop John)
Date: Thu Mar 29 12:26:04 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] BSNL broadband with linux
In-Reply-To: <b2600ec40703271143m68af42a9p2e995a4c06a78f2f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <b2600ec40703270332l5afd9542x3313b764c9f6684f@mail.gmail.com>
	<615164.55583.qm@web50208.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
	<b2600ec40703271143m68af42a9p2e995a4c06a78f2f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <406f1f3f0703282355w248f917et6776c70e55679500@mail.gmail.com>

BSNL gives two types of modems. One is a modem router and the other is
a simple dsl modem. If you have the simple dsl modem then all you have
to do is set up the connection using pppoeconf and then configure to
run "pon <connection name>" when the user logs in or just create a
shortcut on desktop to run a script to run "pon <connection name>".
If you have a modem router then all you have to do is connect to the
router using a browser (http://192.168.1.1 - typically, username
admin, password admin - check the manual for the router to be sure)
and then enter the ISP username and password in the wan configuration
page and you would have an fulltime connected system

From anoopjohn at gmail.com  Thu Mar 29 19:46:54 2007
From: anoopjohn at gmail.com (Anoop John)
Date: Thu Mar 29 19:50:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Internal modems with linux support
Message-ID: <406f1f3f0703290716h3a648dfejacb9ec06a80ef6d2@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Everybody,
We had a discussion in this group some time back regarding internal
modems that are supported in linux. I have found an internal modem
that is supported in linux. The WeP (wipro e-peripherals) Spider 56K
V.92 PCI Modem with the Conexant HSFi CX11252-412 0610y1DB chipset
(PCI ID 14F1:2F30) is supported in linux and it costs only around Rs.
375. The driver from linuxant.com can be installed very easily using
their installer. After some minor settings - username, password, phone
- in wvdial you are ready to go. Only thing is that the speed is
limited to 14kbps for the free version of the driver. The paid version
goes at 20$. I will keep on the lookout for more internal modems that
are supported in linux.
Cheers
Anoop
www.zyxware.com

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Fri Mar 30 10:25:06 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Fri Mar 30 10:25:43 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Open Hardware Needed
Message-ID: <1144.61.247.255.58.1175230506.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

> Is there any online tutorial for Qt?

Try Trolltech's website. http://www.trolltech.com/products/qt

You can try the documentation site: http://doc.trolltech.com/4.2/

Talking about QT licenses, a lot of people don't seem to understand how it
works and so a small writeup is includede below. Admittedly this is some
what offtopic, but in a sense it does focus a bit on opensource
development.. so I state it here.

Here goes:

Please note that the QT license is different from most open source
licenses. Qt comes under a dual licensing policy. Qt Opensource licensing
is available free for opensource development, and Qt commercial licensing
is available for commercial development.

Important:

a) You cannot start developing your product using the QT Opensource
license and then make your product a proprietary product by purchasing a
QT Commercial license later on. Once you have developed code using QT Open
Source license, it will have to remain perpetually under that license.

b) If you decide to purchase QT Commercial license, it is sold per
*developer* and not per seat. That is to say, that if you have a single PC
on which QT is installed and if two people periodically use the same PC
for doing work on QT, you will need to purchase two licenses and not one.

c) Also, QT licenses cannot be transferred between developers more often
than once every 6 months (if I recall correctly). That is to say that if
"Ram" and "Ravi" are two developers for whom you have purchased QT
licenses,  and if "Ram" goes on a holiday or leaves the company, you
cannot bring in a new person and have him use the same QT license -
actually, you can.. but you cannot do this more often than once every 6
months.

d) If you plan to develop across platforms - linux, windows etc, you will
need to buy QT licenses for each such platform.

Regards,
PK
From prem at songbirdtech.com  Fri Mar 30 10:32:24 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)

>> Linux infringes 283 patents, out of which 27 are
>> held by MS.

>No FUD please.

It is not FUD, Linux does violate a number of patents.

>No to software patents:
>http://www.shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/rms.danger.of.software.patents.pdf

I agree.

Talking about patents, pretty much all parts of an OS has been patented in
some way or the other.. so it is really impossible to develop any OS parts
without violating some patent or the other.

But I don't think there is much to worry about this - the big companies
IBM, Oracle, Novell, Redhat, Sun etc have so much invested on Linux that
incase any patent dispute arises, it will be handled in court.

The only danger is if someone inadvertently or deliberately includes code
into the Linux/anyother-OSS-product from some commercial product. That is
something we need to watch out for.

From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Fri Mar 30 11:58:10 2007

In-Reply-To: <1144.61.247.255.58.1175230506.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
References: <1144.61.247.255.58.1175230506.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

Prem Kurian Philip wrote:
>> Is there any online tutorial for Qt?
> 
> Try Trolltech's website. http://www.trolltech.com/products/qt
> 
> You can try the documentation site: http://doc.trolltech.com/4.2/

The best guide I was suggested by Qt Devs and I myself found to be very 
helpful is the Qt Assistant. Better use Qt4 than Qt3 as things to have 
changed a lot.

Qt assistant has in-depth explanation of each class available in Qt, as 
well as it includes a series of 14 tutorials which will give you a good 
confidence of writing Qt code on your own. Also, there are additional 
examples with complete explanation for some real time apps like 
Calculator etc.

Actually, I used the Qt4 assistant tutorial and examples and tried to 
write them in PyQt4 to learn PyQt4.

You can also try out Qt Designer once you have pass through the basic 
knowledge of Qt programming. Do not start with Qt Designer and be 
dependent on it. Just use it as a tool to quickly create UIs while do 
the coding for logic part manually.

From rajaramcomputers at hotmail.com  Sat Mar 31 10:21:06 2007
From: rajaramcomputers at hotmail.com (ramkumar lakshminarayanan)
Date: Sat Mar 31 10:21:22 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Perl Script Execution Error
In-Reply-To: <460B42BA.60708@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <BAY131-F37C8D5693EF5B9E0A9DE9DD620@phx.gbl>

   Dear Friends,

   Thank you all for all the comments regarding the perl script executiion
   error.

   I have made the following modification in my server and it is working.

   It was httpd.conf which was restricting the cgi and perl from getting
   executed.
   I've modified, /usr/local/apache/http/conf/httpd.conf file

   Under ScriptAlias, I've added 2 directory listing
   #
      # "/usr/local/apache/cgi-bin" should be changed to whatever your
   ScriptAliased
      # CGI directory exists, if you have that configured.
      #
       <Directory "/usr/local/apache/cgi-bin">
          AllowOverride None
          Options None
          Order allow,deny
          Allow from all
      </Directory>
   #### UPTO THIS WAS ORIGINAL FOLLOWING WAS ADDED.

      <Directory "/home/rajarams/www/cgi-bin">
          AllowOverride None
          Options +ExecCGI
          AddHandler cgi-script cgi pl
      </Directory>

      <Directory "/home/*/www/cgi-bin">
          AllowOverride None
          Options ExecCGI
          SetHandler cgi-script
      </Directory>

   Then I've restarted the apache services. It is working.

   Regds,

   L.Ramkumar.
